id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class="mw-indicators free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=C-919&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="C-919">C-919</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Narrow-body twinjet airliner by Comac</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:25.5em;border-spacing:2px;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: large; padding-bottom: 0.3em;">C919\n</th></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" China, Ltd.">Commercial Aircraft Corporation of China, Ltd.</a>\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Designer\n</th>\n<td>Wu Guanghui\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>First flight\n</th>\n<td>5 May 2017<sup id="cite_ref-FG170505_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG170505-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Introduction\n</th>\n<td>Planned 2021<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters5feb2018_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters5feb2018-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/OTT_Airlines" title="OTT Airlines">OTT Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-launch_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-launch-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-COMAC-news_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COMAC-news-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<th>Status\n</th>\n<td>Flight testing\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Produced\n</th>\n<td>2011-present\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Number built</span>\n</th>\n<td>6 as of December 2019<sup id="cite_ref-FG191227_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG191227-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Comac C919</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrow-body airliner</a> developed by Chinese aircraft manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Comac" title="Comac">Comac</a>.\nThe development program was launched in 2008. Production of the <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototype</a> began in December 2011, with the first prototype being ready on 2 November 2015 and having its <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">maiden flight</a> on 5 May 2017.\nFirst commercial deliveries of the aircraft are expected in 2021 to <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>.\nThe aircraft, primarily constructed with <a href="/wiki/Aluminium_alloy" title="Aluminium alloy">aluminium alloys</a>, is to be powered by either <a href="/wiki/CFM_International_LEAP" title="CFM International LEAP">CFM International LEAP</a> or <a href="/wiki/ACAE_CJ-1000A" title="ACAE CJ-1000A">ACAE CJ-1000A</a> turbofan engines, and be able to carry 156 to 168 passengers in a normal operating configuration up to 5,555&#160;km (3000 nmi).\nIt is intended to compete primarily with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo_family" title="Airbus A320neo family">Airbus A320neo</a>.\nAs of 31&#160;August&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Comac has 1008 commitments including 305 firm orders, mostly from Chinese leasing companies or airlines.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Naming"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Orders"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Orders</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Specifications"><span <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming">Naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the model number, the <i>C</i> stands for "Comac" or "China"; <i>9</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Homophonic_puns_in_Mandarin_Chinese" class="mw-redirect" title="Homophonic puns in Mandarin Chinese">homophonic pun</a> in Chinese for "forever".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <i>C</i> also has the implication that forms an "ABC" parallel situation with Airbus and Boeing.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COMAC_C919_(4339942885)_extracted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg/220px-COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg/330px-COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg/440px-COMAC_C919_%284339942885%29_extracted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4340" data-file-height="2170" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COMAC_C919_(4339942885)_extracted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Model of the C919 from 2010.</div></div></div>\n<p>The 2008 program launch initially targeted a <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">maiden flight</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ATW170505_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATW170505-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Comac applied for a <a href="/wiki/Type_certificate" title="Type certificate">type certificate</a> for the aircraft from the Civil Aviation Authority of China on 28 October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> At that time the company intended to manufacture up to 2,300 aircraft of the type.<sup id="cite_ref-teal2010_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teal2010-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, COMAC and Irish low-cost airline <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> signed an agreement to co-operate on the development of the C919.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>\' chief strategist <a href="/wiki/Marwan_Lahoud" title="Marwan Lahoud">Marwan Lahoud</a> assumed that the aircraft would offer competition to Airbus by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2010 to 2015 the Chinese cyberthreat actor Turbine Panda, linked to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_State_Security_(China)" title="Ministry of State Security (China)">Ministry of State Security</a>\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> Bureau, penetrated a number of the C919\'s foreign components manufacturers including <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safran" title="Safran">Safran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crowdstrike" class="mw-redirect" title="Crowdstrike">Crowdstrike</a> argued that the operations involved both cyber intrusion and theft as well as <a href="/wiki/HUMINT" class="mw-redirect" title="HUMINT">HUMINT</a> operations with the aim of transitioning component manufacturing to domestic companies using stolen intellectual property and industrial processes.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 November 2011, Comac announced the completion of the joint definition phase, marking the end of the preliminary design phase for the C919, with estimated completion of the detailed design phase in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Production of the first C919 prototype began on 9 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The C919\'s aerodynamics were designed with the help of the <a href="/wiki/Tianhe-2" title="Tianhe-2">Tianhe-2</a> supercomputer.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The annual production was targeted at 150 planes by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Canada\'s <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier Aerospace</a> started collaborating in March 2012 on <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical systems">electrical systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Human interface">human interface</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cockpit" title="Cockpit">cockpit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flight_training" title="Flight training">flight training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flight-test" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight-test">flight-test</a> support, sales, and marketing.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its announced development budget was 58 billion yuan ($9.5 billion) but its actual cost was estimated at well over $20 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek16dec2013_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek16dec2013-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The first prototype was expected to complete final assembly in 2014 and perform its first flight in 2015;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> however, delivery was delayed again until 2018 due to technical difficulties and supply issues.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> At the November 2014 Zhuhai Airshow, it was announced that the first flight would be delayed to 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 2 November 2015, Comac rolled out its first C919 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2018, the development of a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_composite" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon composite">composite</a> wing completed in 2012 was revealed years after abandoning it for a metallic one, as static and damage tolerance tests were completed, verifying the structural design and strength before full-size composite <a href="/wiki/Wingbox" title="Wingbox">wingbox</a> tests.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 12 July, the static test aircraft simulated a 2.5g manoeuvre with a 150% <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_load" title="Ultimate load">ultimate load</a>, bending the wings at the tips by nearly three metres for three seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight13jul2018_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight13jul2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_testing">Flight testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Flight testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg/220px-Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg/330px-Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg/440px-Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="718" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comac_C919_first_vr_test_at_Shanghai_Pudong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first prototype ground tested</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>High-speed taxi tests were completed in April 2017<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and the first flight took place on 5 May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AirlinerWorldOct2019_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirlinerWorldOct2019-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> At the time, Comac had a planned test programme of 4,200 flight hours and introduction to service in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-FG170505_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG170505-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It was estimated that this could be delayed into 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">European Aviation Safety Agency</a> is intended to validate the Chinese type certificate.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek9Jun2017_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek9Jun2017-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\nThe 4,200 hours of testing planned were higher than the 3,000 hours typically required for the Airbus or Boeing narrowbodies, but lower than the 5,000 hours needed for the ARJ21.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight26oct2018_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight26oct2018-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Comac had its second prototype ready on 28 July 2017, aiming to fly it within the year for engine, APU, fuel system and extreme weather tests.\nThe flight-test plan included six aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight31Jul2017_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight31Jul2017-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 28 September, it made its second flight at 10,000&#160;ft (3,000&#160;m), which lasted 2 hours 46 minutes, although it was supposed to last one more hour.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\nThe five-month delay between first and second flights, while the second prototype was being ground-tested, was extraordinary: in 2013 the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350" title="Airbus A350">Airbus A350</a> flew again after five days and in 2015 the troubled <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_MRJ" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitsubishi MRJ">Mitsubishi MRJ</a> flew again after eight days.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 November, it made its third flight in 3h 45min, reaching 3,000&#160;m (9,800&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\nIt was transferred on 10 November from Shanghai to <a href="/wiki/Xian" class="mw-redirect" title="Xian">Xian</a> to continue its flight test program, a 2h 24min, 1,300&#160;km (700&#160;nmi) flight reaching 7,800&#160;m (25,600&#160;ft) and Mach&#160;0.74 (825&#160;km/h; 445&#160;kn).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg/220px-COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg/330px-COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg/440px-COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="730" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COMAC_C919_-_Commercial_Aircraft_Corporation_Of_China_AN4748979.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The second prototype first flight on 17 December 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>The second prototype made its first flight on 17 December 2017. The flight test program allocated the first three prototypes for aircraft performance and engine and power systems testing, the fourth prototype for <a href="/wiki/Avionics" title="Avionics">avionics</a> and electrical system, and the fifth and sixth prototypes for passenger facilities, including the cabin and information system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The delay between first and subsequent flights underlined the program immaturity by maiden flight: flying early at low speed and altitude is possible but faster and higher is limited by <a href="/wiki/Aeroelastic_flutter" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeroelastic flutter">aeroelastic flutter</a> needing ground vibration testing and aircraft instrumentation which were not ready in May.<sup id="cite_ref-Leeham3Jan2018_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leeham3Jan2018-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\nDue to flight testing problems, the 2020 introduction previously scheduled was delayed to 2021, for <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters5feb2018_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters5feb2018-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\nIn February 2018, the first prototype was flying more than once a week.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2018, <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Week" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviation Week">Aviation Week</a> reported flight-test aircraft grounding for modifications, extending the schedule by three months but maintaining a 2020 certification target.\nThe two prototypes needed their <a href="/wiki/Flap_(aeronautics)" title="Flap (aeronautics)">flaps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tailplane" title="Tailplane">tailplanes</a> modified, due to <a href="/wiki/Delamination" title="Delamination">delamination</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Carbon-fiber_reinforced_plastic" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon-fiber reinforced plastic">carbon-fiber reinforced plastic</a> <a href="/wiki/Elevator_(aeronautics)" title="Elevator (aeronautics)">elevators</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek15jun2018_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek15jun2018-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\nThe third test aircraft was also being modified and maximum-rate <a href="/wiki/Cabin_pressurization" title="Cabin pressurization">pressurization</a> was tested.\nAs three other planes will be available in 2019, Comac maintains first deliveries for 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-AirlinerWatch18jun2018_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirlinerWatch18jun2018-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Comac denied any grounding and highlighted that modifications were part of the flight test process, stating the two first aircraft were flying stability tests and checking systems.\nThe first was calibrated and had its counterweight and <a href="/wiki/Trailing_cone" title="Trailing cone">trailing cone</a> systems modified while the second had its functions and systems checked.\nThe third was in final assembly with its wing and fuselage joined, cables and systems were being installed for a first flight target by the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight22jun2018_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight22jun2018-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 12 July, the second prototype flew from <a href="/wiki/Shanghai-Pudong" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai-Pudong">Shanghai-Pudong</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dongying_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dongying Airport">Dongying Airport</a> in 1h 46min to allow for various meteorological conditions testing.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight13jul2018_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight13jul2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nIn September, Comac expected to conduct 1,500 test flights for over 2,000 flying hours before the first delivery and planned to fly the third prototype before the end of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek26sep2018_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek26sep2018-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2018, the flight-deck design was re-evaluated to comply with US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Regulations#Part_25" title="Federal Aviation Regulations">FAR Part 25</a>.1302, not necessary for <a href="/wiki/CAAC" class="mw-redirect" title="CAAC">CAAC</a> but for <a href="/wiki/FAA" class="mw-redirect" title="FAA">FAA</a> certification to sell it outside China, a result of inexperience of the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_design_process" title="Aircraft design process">aircraft design process</a>. Developing a Chinese engine to replace the CFM Leap-1C would take at least another 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\nAt that time the two prototypes had flown less than 150 h, averaging less than 5 h per month each.\nTo achieve certification in December 2020 and first delivery in 2021, the planned 4,200 h of flight tests would need 33 hours a month each if the last four prototypes are evenly spaced before year-end-2019.\nNewest airliner designs like the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350" title="Airbus A350">Airbus A350</a> needed a 2,600 hour test program, and the <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_MRJ" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitsubishi MRJ">Mitsubishi MRJ</a> is expected to need 3,000 h.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek20nov2018_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek20nov2018-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 15, 2018 ten Chinese nationals including intelligence officials were indicted in the US for working with COMAC to steal the secrets of thirteen foreign aerospace companies working on the C919.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of 2018, the first prototype was to enter flutter flight tests after having completed ground tests.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\nThe third prototype made its maiden flight on 28 December for 1h 38 min.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight28dec2018_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight28dec2018-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019">2019</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2019">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A fourth prototype conducted its maiden flight on 1 August 2019 from <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Pudong International Airport">Shanghai Pudong International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight1aug2019_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight1aug2019-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AirlinerWorldOct2019_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirlinerWorldOct2019-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\nA fifth prototype conducted its first flight on 24 October 2019, also from Shanghai airport; the fifth prototype was expected to test for extreme weather conditions, the environmental control system, drainage systems and electrical supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight24oct2019_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight24oct2019-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\nComac rescheduled its certification target from 2020 to 2021, with first delivery the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AirlinerWorldOct2019_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirlinerWorldOct2019-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sixth and final prototype, intended for the flight certification program, completed its maiden flight on December 27, 2019. Reports at the time indicated that the C919 was expected to commence commercial service with China Eastern Airlines in either 2021 or 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-FG191227_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG191227-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2020">2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 27 November 2020, the C919 received its <a href="/w/index.php?title=Type_inspection_authorization&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Type inspection authorization (page does not exist)">type inspection authorization</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Administration_of_China" title="Civil Aviation Administration of China">CAAC</a>, meaning that "the aircraft design has been finalised and verified, and that no major changes can be made to its structure."<sup id="cite_ref-FlGlb27Nov2020_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlGlb27Nov2020-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/COMAC" class="mw-redirect" title="COMAC">COMAC</a> will proceed to more intensive flight tests, to certify its airworthiness by 2021 and to commence deliveries.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2021">2021</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2021">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After completing cold-weather testing in China\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>, the C919 is slated to conduct flight tests in natural <a href="/wiki/Icing_conditions" title="Icing conditions">icing conditions</a> from <a href="/wiki/London_International_Airport" title="London International Airport">London International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ontario,_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Ontario, Canada">Ontario, Canada</a> during March 2021. However, these tests may be delayed depending on the progression of the Covid-19 pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Configuration_and_performance">Configuration and performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Configuration and performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The dimensions of the C919 are quite similar to those of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a>; its <a href="/wiki/Fuselage" title="Fuselage">fuselage</a> is 3.96 metres (13.0&#160;ft) wide and 4.166 metres (13.67&#160;ft) high with a 12.915 square metres (139.02&#160;sq&#160;ft) cross-section. This may allow for a common <a href="/wiki/Unit_load_device" title="Unit load device">unit load device</a> to be used for both aircraft. It has a 33.6 metres (110&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">wingspan</a> (35.4 metres (116&#160;ft) with <a href="/wiki/Winglets" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglets">winglets</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-AW090908_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW090908-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft\'s intended <a href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Payload (air and space craft)">payload capacity</a> will be 20.4 tonnes. The design calls for <a href="/wiki/Cruise_(flight)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruise (flight)">cruise</a> at Mach&#160;0.785 (450&#160;kn; 834&#160;km/h) with an operating <a href="/wiki/Ceiling_(aeronautics)" title="Ceiling (aeronautics)">ceiling</a> of 12,200 metres (39,800 feet). There will be two variants: the standard version with a 4,075&#160;km (2,200&#160;nmi) range, and a 5,555&#160;km (2,999&#160;nmi) extended-range version.<sup id="cite_ref-AW090908_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW090908-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\nThe C919 is a cautious design, similar to the 30 years older A320.<sup id="cite_ref-Leeham3Jan2018_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leeham3Jan2018-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The center wing box, outer wing box, wing panels, flaps, and ailerons are planned to be built in <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi&#39;an">Xi\'an</a>, China; the center fuselage sections are planned to be built in <a href="/wiki/Hongdu" title="Hongdu">Hongdu</a>, China.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aluminium-lithium_alloy" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminium-lithium alloy">Aluminium-lithium alloys</a> account for 8.8% of the structure and <a href="/wiki/Fibre-reinforced_plastic" title="Fibre-reinforced plastic">composite materials</a> for 12%.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The air frame will be made largely of aluminium alloy. Aircraft design and assembly is performed in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wings">Wings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The wing is <a href="/wiki/Supercritical_airfoil" title="Supercritical airfoil">supercritical</a>, increasing aerodynamic efficiency by 20% and reducing drag by 8% compared to a non-supercritical one.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The center wing box was originally intended to use carbon fibre composites.<sup id="cite_ref-teal2010_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teal2010-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It was changed later to an aluminium design to reduce design complications.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG/220px-ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG/330px-ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG/440px-ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4785" data-file-height="3184" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ILA_Berlin_2012_PD_154a.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Environmental_control_system" title="Environmental control system">air conditioning</a> is made by <a href="/wiki/Liebherr" title="Liebherr">Liebherr</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The engine\'s <a href="/wiki/Nacelle" title="Nacelle">nacelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thrust_reverser" class="mw-redirect" title="Thrust reverser">thrust reverser</a> and exhaust system will be provided by <a href="/wiki/Nexcelle" title="Nexcelle">Nexcelle</a>, with such features as an advanced inlet configuration, the extensive use of composites and acoustic treatment and an electrically operated thrust reverser.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a> will supply Air X radial tyres.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\nIts <a href="/wiki/Integrated_modular_avionics" title="Integrated modular avionics">integrated modular avionics</a> architecture is based on <a href="/wiki/Ethernet" title="Ethernet">Ethernet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Leeham3Jan2018_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leeham3Jan2018-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> is made in China by a joint venture of Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Liebherr" title="Liebherr">Liebherr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avic" class="mw-redirect" title="Avic">Avic</a>\'s Landing Gear Advanced Manufacturing Corp: Liebherr LAMC Aviation.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek26sep2018_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek26sep2018-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the <a href="/wiki/Airframe" title="Airframe">airframe</a> is entirely made by Chinese <a href="/wiki/Avic" class="mw-redirect" title="Avic">Avic</a>, most systems are made by Western-Chinese <a href="/wiki/Joint-venture" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint-venture">joint-ventures</a>: with <a href="/wiki/UTC_Aerospace_Systems" title="UTC Aerospace Systems">UTAS</a> for the electric power, fire protection and lighting; with <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_Collins" title="Rockwell Collins">Rockwell Collins</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_cabin" title="Aircraft cabin">cabin</a> systems and <a href="/wiki/Avionics" title="Avionics">avionics</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Thales_Group" title="Thales Group">Thales</a> for the <a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">IFE</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Flight_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight control">flight controls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_power_unit" title="Auxiliary power unit">APU</a>, wheels and brakes; with <a href="/wiki/Moog_Inc." title="Moog Inc.">Moog</a> for the <a href="/wiki/High-lift_device" title="High-lift device">high lift</a> system; with <a href="/wiki/Parker_Hannifin" title="Parker Hannifin">Parker</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Hydraulics" title="Hydraulics">hydraulics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Actuators" class="mw-redirect" title="Actuators">actuators</a> and fuel systems, with Liebherr for the landing gear and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_control_system" title="Environmental control system">air management</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/CFM_International" title="CFM International">CFM</a> engine and Nexcelle nacelle are entirely foreign.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines">Engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Engines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CFM_LEAP-X_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-CFM_LEAP-X_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2906" data-file-height="2071" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CFM_LEAP-X_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CFM_International_LEAP" title="CFM International LEAP">CFM International LEAP</a> mockup</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">Pratt &amp; Whitney</a> and <a href="/wiki/CFM_International" title="CFM International">CFM International</a> proposed engines for the aircraft, the <a href="/wiki/PW1000G" class="mw-redirect" title="PW1000G">PW1000G</a> and <a href="/wiki/CFM_International_LEAP" title="CFM International LEAP">LEAP</a>-1C respectively;<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/CFM_International_LEAP" title="CFM International LEAP">LEAP</a>-1C was selected.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Aviation_Industry_Corporation_of_China" title="Aviation Industry Corporation of China">AVIC</a> Commercial Aircraft Engine Co was also tasked with developing an indigenous engine for the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/ACAE_CJ-1000A" title="ACAE CJ-1000A">ACAE CJ-1000A</a> was unveiled at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai_Airshow" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhuhai Airshow">Zhuhai Airshow</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Assembly of the first CJ-1000AX engine was completed in 18 months in December 2017. The planned entry to service was 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight29dec2017_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight29dec2017-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\nThe engine first ran in May 2018 to 6,600 rpm core speed.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2020, Reuters reported that the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Executive Office of the President of the United States">US government</a> considered blocking <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">GE</a> from selling the LEAP-1C engine to Comac, citing concerns of reverse engineering, competition for <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>, and military use of technology.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> tweeted opposition, saying that national security should not be grounds for trade restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The US eventually granted GE a license to sell the engines.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Market">Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2012 the C919 order book stood at 380 units worth US$26 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and averaging $68.4 million. <a href="/wiki/FlightGlobal" title="FlightGlobal">FlightGlobal</a>\'s Ascend market values in 2013 were $49.2 million for the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320neo">Airbus A320neo</a>, 51% less than its $100.2 million list price and $51.4 million for the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX</a>-8, 49% less than its $100.5 million list price.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Chinese airlines that have placed orders for the C919 already have either the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> or <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a> in their fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Chinese state-owned newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Times" title="Global Times">Global Times</a></i> complained that an <i><a href="/wiki/Aviation_Week" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviation Week">Aviation Week</a></i> editorial about the bleak prospects for the aircraft "maliciously disparaged the future outlook for the C919".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>COMAC aims to take a fifth of the global <a href="/wiki/Narrowbody" class="mw-redirect" title="Narrowbody">narrowbody</a> market and a third of the Chinese market by 2035.<sup id="cite_ref-ATW170505_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATW170505-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It expects 2,000 sales in the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> commented that China considers it as a source of national pride.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> It also claimed the C919 is outdated by 10\xe2\x80\x9315 years compared to the latest versions of the A320 and Boeing 737, and will probably cost more to operate.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\nIts range of 2,200\xe2\x80\x933,000&#160;nmi (4,100\xe2\x80\x935,600&#160;km) falls short of the 3,400 and 3,550&#160;nmi (6,300 and 6,570&#160;km) of the A320neo and 737 Max 8, the C919 <a href="/wiki/Payload-range" class="mw-redirect" title="Payload-range">payload-range</a> and economics are similar to the current single-aisles, but it will compete with the Neo and Max.\n<a href="/wiki/FlightGlobal" title="FlightGlobal">FlightGlobal</a> forecasts 1,209 deliveries: 687 standard and 522 stretched variants, for 85% in China.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight26oct2018_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight26oct2018-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders">Orders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comac_C919&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Orders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>At the November 2010 <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai_Airshow" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhuhai Airshow">Zhuhai Airshow</a>, Comac announced orders for 55 C919 aircraft from six airlines, with an additional 45 options. The purchasing airlines or lessors included <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Development_Bank" title="China Development Bank">CDB</a> Leasing Company, and <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital_Aviation_Services" title="GE Capital Aviation Services">GE Capital Aviation Services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AW101116_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW101116-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On 19 October 2011, Chinese <a href="/wiki/ICBC_Leasing" class="mw-redirect" title="ICBC Leasing">ICBC Leasing</a> ordered 45 C919s and agreed to be the launch customer.<sup id="cite_ref-111019PR_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111019PR-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On 11 November 2014, Comac announced at the 2014 Zhuhai Airshow that <a href="/wiki/China_Merchants_Bank" title="China Merchants Bank">China Merchants Bank</a>\'s aircraft leasing division made a firm commitment for 30 C919s, and that total orders were now up to 450 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-ATW141112_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATW141112-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the June 2015 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a>, Ping An Leasing signed a letter of intent for 50 C919s, becoming one of Comac\'s largest customers, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puren_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puren Group (page does not exist)">Puren Group</a> signed a letter of intent for seven C919s and seven ARJ21s, intended for the start-up Puren Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-FG150615_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG150615-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\nIn November 2016 COMAC has received an order for 20 C919s including 5 firm from <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Pudong_Development_Bank" title="Shanghai Pudong Development Bank">Shanghai Pudong Development Bank</a> Financial Leasing and for 36 C919s from <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Group" title="CITIC Group">CITIC Group</a> Financial Leasing including 18 firm.<sup id="cite_ref-FG161101_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG161101-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\nWhile no down payments were needed before its maiden flight, 500,000 yuan ($76,000) were deposited subsequently for each firm order.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters19sep2017_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters19sep2017-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\nThe last <a href="/wiki/ICBC_Leasing" class="mw-redirect" title="ICBC Leasing">ICBC Leasing</a> order for 55 on 5 December 2017 brought the order book to 785.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters5dec2017_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters5dec2017-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\nIn February 2018, its total order book was for 815, before the order for 200 from <a href="/wiki/HNA_Group" title="HNA Group">HNA Group</a> in June 2018, along with 100 <a href="/wiki/ARJ-21" class="mw-redirect" title="ARJ-21">ARJ-21s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters2jun2018_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters2jun2018-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 31 August 2018, <a href="/wiki/FlightGlobal" title="FlightGlobal">FlightGlobal</a> counts 305 orders plus 45 options and 658 <a href="/wiki/Letters_of_intent" class="mw-redirect" title="Letters of intent">letters of intent</a>: 1008 commitments.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight26oct2018_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight26oct2018-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of March 2020, China Eastern Airlines subsidiary <a href="/wiki/OTT_Airlines" title="OTT Airlines">OTT Airlines</a> is scheduled to be the launch customer for the C919.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-launch_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-launch-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-COMAC-news_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COMAC-news-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<caption>Orders\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Customer\n</th>\n<th>Firm<br
